###Chapter 22

The midday sun beat down on the pavement,but the air in New York still held a crisp, biting chill.
Elisa walked out of the towering glass facade of Aethel Intelligence headquarters. She had just finished a grueling, three-hour architecture review meeting. Her brain was buzzing with code, but her body felt light.
She bought a black coffee from a street vendor.The paper cup was scalding hot against her palm.
She slipped on a pair of oversized, dark sunglasses and blended into the chaotic, rushing river of pedestrians heading toward Central Park. She needed the physical exertion of walking to burn off the residual adrenaline from the meeting.
She entered the park near the south end, following the winding paved paths. The trees were bare, their branches scratching against the pale blue sky.
As she approached the wide, open expanse of Sheep Meadow, a sharp, obnoxious sound cut through the ambient noise of the park.
It was the loud, screeching laugh of a child.
Elisa slowed her pace. She turned her head toward the sound.
Through a gap in the skeletal bushes, she saw three figures standing near a wooden park bench.
Her stomach immediately contracted into a tight,painful knot.
August was standing there. He was wearing a casual, incredibly expensive navy cashmere overcoat. He was holding a large, brightly colored kite.
He was leaning down, patiently untangling the thick white string for a young boy.
Allena was standing right next to him. She had her arm looped tightly through August's elbow.She was wearing a soft pink wool coat,smiling brightly,playing the role of the perfect, loving maternal figure.
The boy was Tate Mills. Allena's younger brother.He was about seven or eight years old, and he was infamous in the elite Manhattan private school circles for being an absolute terror.
Tate let out another screeching laugh. He violently snatched the plastic string spool right out of August's hands.
The sudden, aggressive movement caused Tate to stumble backward. He crashed directly into a passing jogger.
The jogger, a man in a grey hoodie, spilled his water bottle down his own shirt.
"Hey! Watch it, kid!" the jogger snapped, glaring at Tate.
Before the jogger could take another step, a massive man in a dark suit stepped out from behind
a nearby oak tree. It was one of August's private security detail.
The bodyguard didn't say a word. He just stared at the jogger, his hand resting subtly over the distinct bulge of a firearm beneath his jacket.
The jogger's eyes widened in fear. He swallowved his anger, backed away, and quickly jogged off in the opposite direction.
August didn't scold Tate. He didn't tell him to apologize.
Instead, August chuckled. He reached out and affectionately ruffled Tate's hair.
"Lots of energy today, buddy," August said, his voice rich with indulgence.
Elisa stood frozen in the shadow of a large elm tree.
She stared at the man who had once pinned her against a wall, his eyes dark with rage, threatening to destroy her life if she ever got pregnant. She stared at the man who had called children 'parasites' that would ruin his empire.
Now, he was standing in a public park, playing the doting, patient father figure to his mistress's bratty brother.
Elisa squeezed the paper coffee cup in her hand.The scalding liquid sloshed against the plastic lid,burning her skin, but she welcomed the pain.It grounded her.
A wave of pure, physiological nausea rolled
through her digestive tract. It wasn't heartbreak. It was the absolute disgust of witnessing a hypocrite in his natural element.
Suddenly, her secondary, encrypted phone vibrated in her trench coat pocket.
She pulled it out. It was a message from Jewel.Jewel had sent a screenshot from Instagram.
Elisa tapped the image. It was a post from a highly exclusive, private account run by a prominent Upper East Side socialite.
The photo was a candid,zoomed-in shot of August,Allena, and Tate in the park, taken from a distance just moments ago.
The caption read: Mr. Chambers practicing his fatherly duties! The century wedding is definitely coming.Such a beautiful, real family.
Elisa scrolled down. The comments were a toxic sludge of sycophancy and cruelty.
'They look so perfect together. Allena is glowing.''Thank god he's finally getting rid of that barren,toxic nurse. Imagine being married for seven years and not being able to give a man like August a child.Useless.'
Elisa stared at the glowing screen. The words didn't hurt her. They just confirmed that the entire social ecosystem around August was a diseased swamp.
She swiped her thumb across the screen,permanently blocking the socialite's account.
She shoved the phone back into her pocket and looked up.
Tate was jumping up and down, pointing a demanding finger toward a luxury ice cream cart parked fifty yards away.
"I want vanilla! The expensive one! Go get it!" Tate yelled at August, treating the billionaire like an errand boy.
August actually smiled. He nodded obediently.
"Alright, alright. Hold the kite," August said.
He turned away from Allena and Tate, beginning to walk toward the ice cream cart.
As August turned, his gaze swept across the tree line.
His eyes passed over the elm tree. Then, they snapped back.
He stopped walking.
Elisa didn't hide. She stood perfectly still in the shadows. The collar of her grey trench coat was popped up, and the dark sunglasses hid her eyes,but her posture was unmistakable.
She stared directly at him. Her gaze was like a physical weight, heavy and completely dead. She looked at himn the way a coroner looks at a corpse on a steel table.
August's chest hitched. A sudden, violent jolt of electricity shot down his spine.
His eyebrows slammed together. He squinted,
trying to pierce the shadows and confirm it was her.But Elisa was already moving.
She turned on her heel with military precision.She walked away, her strides long and purposeful,instantly vanishing into a thick crowd of tourists taking photos of the skyline.
August took a step toward the trees, his heart suddenly hammering against his ribs.
His hand flew to his right wrist. His fingers frantically twisted the platinum cufflink,a desperate,subconscious attempt to ground himself.
A suffocating wave of panic washed over him. He had no control over her anymore. She was a ghost haunting his periphery, and her absolute silence was driving him insane.
"August?" Allena called out, her voice whiny. She jogged over and wrapped her arms around his waist."What's wrong? Why did you stop?"
August tore his eyes away from the empty tree line. He forced his breathing to slow down.
"Nothing," August muttered, his voice tight. "Just thought I saw someone."
He pulled away from Allena's grip and continued walking toward the cart, his mood completely ruined.
Elisa walked rapidly until she reached the park exit at 59th Street.
She stopped at a metal trash can. She lifted her
hand and dropped the full, lukewarm cup of coffee into the garbage.
She pulled out her encrypted phone and dialed the direct line to Harvey Vance, the Aethel lawyer.
The line clicked open.
"Ms. Faye," Vance's voice was crisp.
"Is the agreement drafted?" Elisa demanded.Her voice was a blade of solid ice.

"We are finalizing the Latin legal nesting clauses now," Vance replied.
"Finish it," Elisa ordered. "I need it in my hands today."
###Chapter 23

The call from Germaine had been as predictable as it was imperious. Less than an hour after her confrontation with August in the park, Elisa was summoned to the Long Island estate like a disobedient servant. The yellow taxi rattled as it merged onto the private, tree-lined road leading to the Chambers family's LongIsland estate.
Elisa sat in the back, staring blankly at the passing ancient oaks.
Suddenly,the taxi slammed on its brakes. The tires shrieked against the asphalt.
Elisa was thrown forward, her seatbelt biting sharply into her collarbone.
A massive, black Range Rover with tinted windows and government-style license plates had swerved directly across the road, violently cutting off the taxi.
Before the terrified taxi driver could even honk, the doors of the Range Rover flew open.
Two men in identical dark suits stepped out. They didn't look like standard bodyguards;they moved with the cold, mechanical precision of paramilitary operators.
One of them marched straight to the back door of the taxi and ripped it open.
"Ms. Wilder," the security chief said. His voice was flat, offering no respect. He deliberately used her maiden name. "Madame Germaine requires your presence in the main house. Immediately. It concerns the public relations disaster you caused at the gala."
Elisa looked at the man's large hand gripping the door frame.
She didn't argue. She didn't panic. She knew fighting Germaine's thugs on a private road was pointless.
She calmly reached into her purse, pulled out a twenty-dollar bill, and handed it to the shaking driver.
She stepped out of the taxi. Her black stiletto heels crunched against the gravel.
She ignored the security guards completely,walking past them with her chin held high.
She navigated the sprawling, perfectly manicured French maze garden. The towering hedges felt like prison walls. She approached the massive, gothic-style main house. The grey stone absorbed the sunlight,radiating a cold, oppressive energy.
A maid silently opened the heavy oak front doors.
Elisa stepped into the grand foyer. The air smelled of old money,beeswax polish, and decay.①
She walked toward the main parlor.
The second her foot crossed the threshold into the room, a sharp whistling sound cut through the air.
Elisa instinctively jerked her head to the left.
A delicate, incredibly expensive Wedgwood porcelain teacup flew past her ear. It smashed violently against the wooden doorframe behind her,exploding into a hundred razor-sharp shards.
Fine porcelain dust rained down on her shoulder.
"You vicious,attention-seeking whore!"
Meredith Hastings was standing in the center of the parlor. Her face was contorted into a mask of absolute, screaming fury. Her chest heaved under her silk blouse.
"You couldn't stand it, could you?!" Meredith shrieked, pointing a shaking finger at Elisa."You saw Allena getting the respect she deserves, and you had to play the hero! You embarrassed her in front of the entire medical board!"
Elisa stood perfectly still amidst the broken porcelain. She didn't flinch. She didn't even blink.
"Because of your little stunt," Meredith screamed,taking a step closer, "the underground blogs are calling Allena a fraud! And August is taking it out on my son! Julian's trust fund is frozen because of you!"Elisa looked at the hysterical woman.
A cold, mocking smile touched the corners of Elisa's lips.
"Are you finished?" Elisa asked. Her voice was dangerously quiet, cutting through Meredith's screaming like a scalpel.
Meredith stopped, panting heavily.
"Your son is a useless parasite," Elisa said, her words dripping with pure contempt. "And that fake docto you're all protecting is a lethal idiot. Do you really think I give a damn about your family's pathetic internal politics?"
The absolute disrespect in Elisa's voice hit Meredith like a physical blow.
Meredith let out a feral screech. She lunged forward,raising her right hand high, aiming a vicious,open-handed slap directly at Elisa's face.
Elisa was ready.
She didn't block it this time. She didn't step back.
Elisa planted her feet, twisted her hips, and swung her own left hand in a brutal, lightning-fast arc.
Crack.
The sound of the slap echoed like a gunshot in the cavernous parlor.
Elisa's palm connected solidly with Meredith's perfectly powdered cheek. The kinetic force of the blow was immense.
Meredith's head snapped to the side.She lost her balance, her expensive heels twisting under her weight. She crashed hard onto the Persian rug,clutching her face, her eyes wide with absolute,paralyzed shock.
"What the hell is going on here?!"
A voice roared from the grand staircase.
August was taking the stairs two at a time. He was wearing a dark, unbuttoned dress shirt, his face dark with fury.
He had heard the crash of the teacup and the sharp crack of the slap.
He stormed into the parlor. He saw his aunt sprawled on the floor, a bright red handprint blooming on her cheek. And he sawElisa standing over her, looking completely unbothered.
August rushed forward and grabbed Meredith by the arm,hauling her up from the floor.
He turned his head, fixing Elisa with a glare of pure,concentrated hatred.
His eyes flickered to the shattered porcelain on the floor, then back to Elisa's cold face. "Not only do you assault my family," he snarled, his voice vibrating with rage, "you come into my family's home and destroy it? Are you completely out of your mind? You are a psychotic bitch."
Elisa looked at her husband.
She looked at the man who always, without fail,arrived at the end of a conflict and immediately convicted her without asking a single question.
She felt a strange sensation in her chest. It wasn't anger. It was profound, exhausting boredom.
She didn't defend herself. She didn't explain that Meredith threw a cup at her head. It didn't matter anymore.
Elisa slowly opened her leather clutch.
She pulled out a small, individually wrapped sanitizing wet wipe.
She tore the foil packet open. She pulled out the alcohol-soaked cloth.
While maintaining dead eye contact with August,Elisa began to slowly,meticulously wipe down the palm and fingers of her left hand-the hand that had just struck his aunt.
She wiped it as if she had just touched raw sewage.
The sheer, staggering level of physical disgust in her action hit August harder than a punch to the throat.
His jaw dropped slightly. The angry words died on his tongue.
"I'm going to have you thrown out of New York!"Meredith sobbed, hiding behind August's broad shoulder.
August's rage reignited. He dropped Meredith's arm and took a menacing step toward Elisa, reaching out to grab her wrist.
Elisa stopped wiping her hand.
Her eyes turned into black ice.
"Touch me," Elisa whispered, her voice dropping to a lethal, vibrating frequency. "Touch me, August,and I will walk straight out of this house and file a police report for assault. I will drag your precious name through a criminal court."
August's hand froze in mid-air.
He stared at her. The woman standing in front of him was a complete stranger. The submissive,eager-to-please wife was dead. This woman was a predator, and she was entirely unafraid of him.
A cold, sickening wave of powerlessness washed over August. His fingers twitched.
Elisa crumpled the used wet wipe into a ball.
She tossed it perfectly into a crystal wastebasket near the sofa.
"I'm going to see your mother now," Elisa said,her voice flat. "Try to keep the trash off the floor while I'm gone."
She turned her back on him and walked out of the parlor, heading down the long hallway toward Germaine's study.
August stood frozen on the Persian rug.
He listened to the sharp, steady click of her heels fading away.
He realized, with a sudden, terrifying clarity, that she wasn't throwing a tantrum. She wasn't trying to make him jealous.
She truly, completely, did not care if he existed.
His chest tightened painfully. He couldn't breathe.
###Chapter 24

The air inside Germaine Chambers' study was thick and suffocating, smelling of aged leather,expensive cigar smoke, and old paper.
Elisa pushed open the heavy oak door and stepped inside.
Germaine was sitting behind a massive mahogany desk. She was wearing a rigid, dark green suit. She was aggressively flipping through a thick stack of political polling data.
She didn't look up when Elisa entered. She simply raised one manicured finger and pointed to a stiff,wooden guest chair opposite the desk.
Elisa didn't sit.
She walked right up to the edge of the desk,crossed her arms over her chest, and looked down at the matriarch.
Germaine finally stopped reading. She slowly closed the file, intertwining her fingers on the polished wood. She looked up,her cold,calculating eyes sweeping over Elisa's sharp suit and defiant posture.
"Your little stunt at the hospital gala was a disaster,"Germaine stated,her voice devoid of any inflection."The media is digging into August's personal life.The rumors about your marriage failing are
affecting the poll numbers for Senator Hayes. We are his primary donors. I will not allow your domestic drama to cost us a Senate seat."
Elisa stared at her. "Get to the point."
Germaine's eyes narrowed at the disrespect.
"Next month is the Senator's primary fundraising gala," Germaine commanded."You will attend.You will wear the Chambers diamonds. You will stand next to August, you will hold his hand,and you will smile for the cameras. You will play the perfect,loving wife until the election is over."
Elisa let out a short, harsh laugh.
"I asked August for a divorce," Elisa said,her voice ringing with absolute finality. "I am not playing dress-up for your political theater."
Germaine slammed her open palm flat against the desk. The sound cracked like a whip.
"Do not use that word in this house!" Germaine hissed,her aristocratic mask slipping for a second."You do not dictate terms to this family. You are a Chambers by marriage, and you will remain one until I decide you are no longer useful. You will not get a divorce unless I allow it."
Elisa's brain, trained to process complex Al logic trees, instantly analyzed the variables in Germaine's threat.
Germaine was desperate for a public display of unity. She needed Elisa to cooperate.
This was the perfect leverage.
Elisa's cold smile vanished. She dropped her arms and leaned slightly over the desk, adopting the posture of a ruthless negotiator.
"Fine," Elisa said smoothly. "I'll play the loving wife.I'll smile for the cameras. But my acting fee has gone up."
Germaine scoffed, a look of profound disgust crossing her face. "I knew it. You're just holding out for more money.How predictable."
"I want the Hamptons property," Elisa demanded,ignoring the insult. "The oceanfront estate in East Hampton. I want the deed transferred entirely to my name, free and clear of the family trust.Unfreeze the transaction protocols today."
Germaine frowned deeply. She studied Elisa's face,trying to find the trick.
Why a house? Why now?
But Germaine's inherent class prejudice blinded her.She truly believed Elisa was just a greedy,lower-class opportunist trying to secure a golden parachute before the marriage inevitably imploded.
"You are a parasite," Germaine sneered. "But fine.If a piece of real estate buys your obedience for the next month,you can have it."
Germaine reached out and pressed a silver button on her desk phone, activating the speaker. She dialed August's internal extension.
The phone rang twice.
"What?" August's voice snapped through the
speaker. He sounded incredibly agitated, likely still reeling from the confrontation in the parlor.
"Elisa is in my study," Germaine said coldly. "She claims you two are actively discussing divorce. Is this true?"
The study was dead silent. Elisa stopped breathing.She stared at the black plastic of the speakerphone,her heart hammering against her ribs.
A harsh,cruel laugh echoed from the speaker.
"Divorce?" August mocked, his voice dripping with pure arrogance. "She's throwing a tantrum, Mother.She's using the word to get attention because she's jealous of Allena. She would never walk away from my money."
"She said she gave you papers," Germaine pressed."I didn't even read them," August scoffed dismissively. "I told Brenda to file that garbage away. I never gave it a second thought. It'sover.Don't let her manipulate you."
Elisa's stomach dropped, and then, a massive,overwhelming surge of pure adrenaline flooded her veins.
He didn't even remember.
He had dismissed the fake divorce papers she had given him, but in his arrogance, he had also forgotten about the original,seven-year prenuptial agreement. He didn't realize the clock was ticking down to zero without requiring his signature at all He was completely, utterly blind.
"Good," Germaine said, her lips curling into a victorious smirk. She hung up the phone.
She looked up at Elisa, her eyes filled with triumphant mockery.
"Your little bluff has been called," Germaine said."He doesn't care. Now, you will attend the gala."
Elisa lowered her eyes, deliberately hiding the lethal, predatory gleam that had just ignited in them.
She forced her shoulders to slump slightly,feigning defeat.
"I'll attend," Elisa said softly, playing the beaten wife perfectly. "But I still want the house. I'll go to Wall Street tomorrow and make August sign the property transfer papers myself. Consider it my down payment for the gala."
Germaine waved her hand dismissively, already bored with the conversation. "Do whatever you want. Just don't embarrass me again."
Elisa turned and walked toward the door.
The moment her hand touched the brass doorknob,the mask of defeat vanished.
Her face hardened into a mask of terrifying,absolute resolve.
She had her excuse. She had a legitimate,Germaine-approved reason to shove a massive stack of legal documents right under August's nose.
The trap was set.
###Chapter 25

The next morning, the sky over Manhattan was a bruised,heavy grey.
Elisa walked into the towering glass lobby of Aethel Intelligence in the Financial District. She bypassed her usual route to the R&D labs and took the secure elevator directly to the 40th floor-the legal department.
The doors opened to a silent, sterile hallway lined with frosted glass walls.
She walked into Conference Room B.
Harvey Vance, a man in a razor-sharp bespoke suit with silver hair and gold-rimmed glasses, was already sitting at the long marble table.
He slid a thick, beautifully bound legal document across the table toward her.
The cover page read in bold, elegant font: Deed of Transfer and Trust Yield Reallocation: East Hampton Estate.
Elisa sat down. She didn't look at the cover. She immediately flipped open the thick stack of premium paper.
"Page thirty-seven," Vance said quietly, tapping his gold pen against the table.
Elisa turned to page thirty-seven.
The text here was a dense, suffocating wall of
legal jargon. It was formatted in a slightly smaller font,buried deep within a section detailing 'Liability Waivers and Future Claims.'
Elisa's eyes scanned the text.
It was a masterpiece of deception. Vance had used archaic Latin legal phrasing and triple-nested subordinate clauses. To a casual reader, it looked like standard boilerplate language protecting the property from future inheritance disputes.
But buried in the center of the paragraph were the lethal words.the signatory hereby irrevocably waives, relinquishes, and permanently surrenders any and all paternal claims, custody rights,visitation privileges, and legal standing regarding the minor child, Kayden Gilmore,born...
Elisa checked the spelling of Kayden's name.She checked the date of birth. Every single letter was perfect.
"Unless he is a specialist in family law actively looking for a custody trap," Vance said, adjusting his glasses, "his brain will automatically skip over this section due to reading fatigue. It is legally binding and practically invisible."
Elisa closed the document.
She pulled a heavy,brown leather envelope from her bag. It had the official Chambers Group Legal Department seal stamped on the front. She had taken it from the penthouse months ago.
She slid the deadly document into the Chambers
envelope, sealing the clasp. The camouflage was complete.
"Thank you, Harvey," Elisa said.
She stood up, clutching the envelope to her chest,and walked out of the conference room.

As she walked down the silent hallway,her encrypted phone buzzed with a priority alert from Jewel. She stepped into a deserted alcove overlooking the city and opened the message. It wasn't text. It was a single, heavily compressed audio file.
Elisa slipped a wireless earbud into her ear and hit play. The sound was distorted, clearly recorded in a loud, crowded bar, but the voices were unmistakable.
First, Julian Hastings, his speech slurred with alcohol. "She's a parasite!" he slurred, his voice cracking with impotent rage. "A goddamn parasite who stole another woman's bed! That's all she is!"
Then, a second fileplayed. This one was a crystal -clear recording of a phone call Jewel had intercepted from a shell company server. It was Simon, August's assistant, speaking to a private investigator.
"Mr.Chambers' orders are absolute," Simon's voice was cold and precise. "Liquidate all of Mr. Hastings'offshore assets. Revoke his credit lines. Contact the board of his tech startup and inform them his family funding has been permanently severed.He wants him socially and financially executed by
morning. The reason? Insulting Ms. Mills."
The audio ended. Elisa stood motionless, staring out at the grey skyline. The earbud in her ear felt like a shard of ice.
She knew August was ruthless in business. She knew he was a narcissist.
But this... this was the action of a sociopath. He had financially and socially executed his own blood relative, his own cousin, simply for hurting his mistress's feelings.
Elisa looked down at the brown envelope in her hands.
Her fingers began to tremble, but she quickly clenched them into tight fists, crushing the edges of the leather.
If August ever found out about Kayden...
If Kayden ever existed in his world, and she accidentally annoyed Allena, or if Allena felt threatened by a legitimate heir... August wouldn't hesitate. He would crush a five-year-old girl with the same cold, mechanical brutality he used to crush his cousin.
The last microscopic, lingering shadow of guilt Elisa felt about deceiving him vanished instantly. It was burned away by a raging, protective maternal fire.
She wasn't just stealing a signature. She was building a fortress to keep a monster away from her child.
Elisa pushed away from the wall. Her posture was
rigid, her eyes burning with a terrifying, absolute clarity.
She walked to the elevator and hit the down button.She pulled out her phone and opened her messages. She typed a text to Simon, August's executive assistant.
I am arriving at HQ in ten minutes. Tell August to have his pen ready. I'm getting the Hamptons property signed over,per Germaine's orders. Do not make me wait.
She hit send.
The elevator doors opened. Elisa stepped inside.descending toward Wall Street to execute the kill.
###Chapter 26

The black Maybach pulled up to the curb outside the towering, monolithic glass skyscraper that housed the Chambers Group headquarters on Wall Street.
Elisa stepped out. The wind howled through the concrete canyon, but she didn't button her coat.She held the brown leather envelope tightly against her side.
She walked through the revolving doors into the massive,thirty-foot-high marble lobby.
Usually, when she came here, she kept her head down, using the private executive elevator in the back to avoid drawing attention.
Not today.
She walked straight across the center of the lobby,the sharp click of her heels echoing off the marble walls.
She approached the main reception desk. The head receptionist, a woman who had always looked at Elisa with thinly veiled pity and disdain, immediately stood up, raising a hand to stop her.
"Mrs. Chambers, you can't go up," the receptionist said, her tone condescending. "Simon did inform us of your arrival, but Mr. Chambers is on a critical overseas call and reiterated that no one was to go
up under any circumstances. My apologies, but my hands are tied."
Elisa didn't stop walking.
She locked eyes with the receptionist, her gaze so cold and piercing that the woman physically flinched.
"I.am here on the direct orders of Madame Germaine," Elisa said, her voice echoing loudly enough for the nearby security guards to hear. She raised the brown envelope with the Chambers Legal seal. "Unless you want to call Germaine and tell her you're blocking her political assets, I suggest you step aside."
The receptionist's face paled at the mention of the matriarch. She quickly lowered her hand and stepped back.
Elisa swiped her biometric ring against the scanner.The private elevator doors slid open.
She stepped in and hit the button for the 68th floor.
The elevator shot upward, the pressure popping in her ears.
When the doors opened, the atmosphere on the executive floor was suffocatingly tense. The air smelled of ozone, expensive cologne, and high-stakes panic.
Simon,August's executive assistant, was pacing the hallway. When he saw Elisa step out, his eyes widened in panic.
He rushed forward,physically blocking the hallway leading to the CEO's office.
"Elisa, you cannot be here," Simon hissed, keeping his voice low. "He is in the middle of a ten-billion -dollar cross-border acquisition call with the Frankfurt board. It's a video conference. If you interrupt him, he will fire everyone on this floor."
Elisa stopped. She looked at her wristwatch.
"I have a meeting at Aethel in forty minutes," Elisa said flatly. "He has exactly ten minutes to sign this property transfer, or I call Germaine and tell her the deal is off."
Simon sneered, his loyalty to August making him arrogant. "You really think you can strong-arm him with a house?"
Elisa ignored Simon completely. She sidestepped him with fluid grace and walked straight down the hallway toward the massive, soundproof glass conference room.
Through the floor-to-ceiling glass walls, she saw August.
He was standing at the head of a long obsidian table, his back to the window. He was wearing a stark white dress shirt, the sleeves rolled up,exposing his muscular forearms. He was speaking rapid, aggressive German into a high-end microphone, dominating the executives on the massive video screens.
Elisa walked right up to the glass wall.
She didn't knock. She didn't wave.
She simply sat down on the sleek leather waiting sofa positioned directly outside the glass. She crossed her legs, placed the brown envelope on her lap, and pulled out her phone.
Inside the room, August felt a shift in the light.
He turned his head slightly.
His eyes locked onto Elisa sitting just beyond the glass.
For a split second, his powerful, commanding posture faltered. He was shocked she had bypassed security.
Then, his eyes narrowed into slits of pure, arrogant defiance.
He decided to play his favorite game: psychological annihilation through absolute ignorance.
He turned his head back to the screens. He deliberately raised his voice, continuing his German presentation, completely acting as if the woman sitting ten feet away was entirely invisible. It was a power move designed to make her feel small,needy,and pathetic.
Elisa didn't even look up.
She opened an email from Alastair regarding the Chiron server migration. She began typing a complex technical response, her thumbs flying across the screen. Her face was a mask of absolute,serene focus.
Five minutes passed.
August was speaking, but his peripheral vision was entirely consumed by the grey suit outside the glass.
He waited for her to look up. He waited for her to fidget, to show anger, to show something.
She didn't. She was completely engrossed in her phone, utterly indifferent to his display of power.
A dark, irrational irritation began to boil in August's chest.
His right hand dropped from the table. His fingers found his platinum cufflink. He began to twist it,the metal grinding against his skin.
"Herr Chambers?" one of the German executives asked through the speakers, looking confused.
August realized he had stopped speaking mid-sentence. His brain had short-circuited, entirely distracted by the woman ignoring him.
His face flushed with sudden, hot embarrassment and rage.
He violently slammed his hand flat on the table.
"W/e will reconvene in one hour," August barked in English, cutting the feed instantly. The screens went black.
The heavy glass doors of the conference room slid open with a pneumatic hiss.
August stormed out. He radiated a dark,suffocating menace. He stopped directly in front of
Elisa, his massive frame blocking the overhead lights, casting her in shadow.
"You have exactly ten seconds to explain why you are interrupting a ten-billion-dollar merger,"August snarled, his voice a lethal whisper, "before I have security drag you out by your hair."
Elisa hit 'send' on her email.
She locked her phone, slipped it into her pocket,and slowly raised her head.
Her eyes met his. They were completely dead.
"Ten seconds is all I need," she said.
###Chapter 27

Elisa didn't stand up. She remained seated on the leather sofa, forcing August to look down at her,a subtle rejection of his physical intimidation.
She picked up the brown leather envelope from her lap.
With a swift, fluid motion, she pulled out the thick stack of legal documents and tossed them onto the low glass coffee table between them. The heavy paper hit the glass with a solid,echoing thud.
"Germaine wants her politicaL theater," Elisa said,her voice dripping with bored contempt. "I want my payment. Sign the transfer for the Hamptons house,and I'll leave you to your little phone calls."
August stared at the documents.
His jaw clenched. The sheer audacity of her transaction-treating their marriage like a cheap hostage negotiation-infuriated him.
He let out a harsh, mocking laugh.
"So, the mask finally slips," August sneered, his eyes filled with absolute disgust. "All that self-righteous anger at the hospital, all that fake outrage about Allena... and it all just comes down to a piece of real estate. You really are just a greedy,pathetic gold digger."
Elisa shrugged her shoulders slightly.
"If you're going to treat me like a whore, August,"she said, her voice perfectly steady, "I might as well get paid like a high-end one. Sign the paper."
The insult to herself was a calculated move. It perfectly fed his confirmation bias. It made him feel superior.
August sneered again. He bent down, snatched the thick document off the table, and turned on his heel, marching straight into his private CEO office.
Elisa stood up and followed him inside.
Simon hovered nervously by the open door,watching them like a hawk.
August threw the document onto his massive obsidian desk. He dropped into his high-backed leather chair. He reached out and pulled a heavy,black Montblanc fountain pen from its holder. He uncapped it with a sharp click.
Elisa stood on the opposite side of the desk.
Her heart began to beat faster. The rhythmic thudding echoed in her ears. She locked her knees to stop them from trembling. She forced her breathing to remain shallow and silent.
August moved his pen toward the signature line on the final page.
Then,he stopped.
The nib of the pen hovered a millimeter above the paper.
August was a predator in the financial world.He
had survived by being paranoid. A sudden,instinctual itch crawled up the back of his neck.
He slowly raised his head. His dark, piercing eyes locked onto Elisa's face.
"You seem very eager to get out of here," August said, his voice dropping an octave, heavy with sudden suspicion. "And you brought this directly from Germaine? Not through my legal team?"
Elisa's stomach plummeted into a bottomless void.He's going to read it.
She dug her fingernails brutally into the palms of her hands, using the physical pain to anchor her facial muscles.
She let out a loud, exaggerated sigh and rolled her eyes.
"It has the Chambers Legal seal right on the envelope, August," Elisa said, injecting her voice with maximum annoyance. "It's your family's standard boilerplate trust transfer. What do you think I did? Hacked your lawyers and rewrote it? I'm a nurse. If you're that terrified of a piece of paper,call your legal team and have them read it to you like a bedtime story."
The insult hit its mark.
August's eyes flashed with anger. His massive ego couldn't handle being called a coward by a woman he considered intellectually inferior.
"I don't need my lawyers to spot a rat," August growled.
He didn't sign.
Instead,he flipped the massive document back to page one.
He began to read.
The office fell into a terrifying, suffocating silence.The only sound was the sharp swish of the heavy paper as August turned the pages.
Page five. Page ten.
August was a speed reader. He consumed complex legal jargon for breakfast. His eyes darted back and forth across the text with terrifying efficiency.
Elisa felt a cold bead of sweat slide down her spine,soaking into her silk blouse.
Page fifteen.Page twenty.
Every time a page turned, it felt like a physical blow to her chest. The bomb was on page thirty-seven.The moment his eyes hit that Latin phrasing, he would know. He would know she was hiding a child.He would destroy her.
Page twenty-five.Page thirty.
August suddenly frowned. His eyes stopped moving.He stared hard at a paragraph near the bottom of page thirty.
He tapped the nib of his Montblanc pen against the desk. Tap. Tap. Tap.
He opened his mouth, drawing in a breat to ask a question about the trust yield structure.
BANG.
The heavy, soundproof oak door of the office was violently thrown open. It crashed against the wall.
Simon practically fell into the room. His face was chalk-white, his tie askew, and he was panting heavily.
August's head snapped up. His eyes blazed with lethal fury at the interruption.
"What the hell is wrong with you, Simon?!" August roared.
Simon swallowed hard, his hands shaking as he held up his phone.
"Sir," Simon gasped, his voice cracking. "It's Allena.She was at Carnegie Hall for a charity photoshoot.The scaffolding gave way. She fell off the stage."
August froze.
The color drained completely from his face.
His hand clenched into a tight fist around the heavy barrel of the pen, and in the sudden, convulsive movement, the sharp nib dragged violently across page thirty, tearing a jagged, bleeding slash of black ink through the dense text.
"ls she alive?" August whispered, his voice trembling with a terror Elisa had never heard before.
"She's conscious, but she can't move her right leg,"Simon said rapidly. "The paramedics are taking her to the VIPER at Presbyterian."
August shot out of his chair. The heavy leather seat rolled backward and crashed into the window.
The document, the property, the suspicion-everything vanished from his mind. He was completely consumed by panic.
###Chapter 28

August lunged across the office,grabbing Simon by the lapels of his suit jacket.
"Did you call the chief of surgery?!" August roared,saliva flying from his lips. "Get the helicopter ready!If there's traffic, we fly her out!"
"I've already alerted the hospital, sir," Simon stammered, terrified by the sheer violence in August's grip. "The car is waiting downstairs."
August shoved Simon aside. He grabbed his suit jacket from the back of a chair and snatched his car keys off the desk.
He didn't even glance at the desk. He was already moving toward the door, his mind entirely focused on Allena's broken body.
Elisa watched him.
Her heart was beating so violently it felt like it was going to crack her ribs.
This was it. The window of opportunity was closing in seconds. If he walked out that door, the document would be sent to his legal team for review later. The trap would be discovered.
She had to force his hand right now.
As August took his first step toward the hallway,Elisa slammed her left hand down flat on top of the legal document.
"August!" Elisa shouted. Her voice was sharp, loud,and completely devoid of empathy.
August stopped in the doorway. He whipped his head around, his eyes wild and bloodshot.
"What?!" he snarled, looking at her as if she were an insect blocking his path.
"I don't care if your mistress broke her neck," Elisa said, her words dripping with absolute, freezing cruelty. "You are not leaving this room until you sign this paper."
August stared at her in sheer disbelief.
"Allena is in an ambulance," August yelled, his voice echoing in the hallway. "She could be bleeding internally, and you want me to sign a real estate transfer?! Are you a sociopath?!"
Elisa didn't flinch. She leaned her weight onto her hand, pressing the document firmly against the desk.
"I am a woman who wants her property," Elisa shot back, her eyes locking onto his with terrifying intensity. She deliberately raised her left wrist,looking at her watch. "You have thirty seconds.If you walk out that door without signing,I am calling Germaine. I will tell her the deal is off.I will not attend the gala. I will call Page Six the second I step into the elevator. I will give them every sordid,pathetic detail of your affair while your precious Allena is lying in a hospital bed. Your mother's election campaign will be absolutely ruined by the scandal before the sun goes down."
The threat hit August like a physical wall.
He knew, his mother. If Elisa boycotted the gala and filed for a messy divorce now, Germaine would be furious. The family would blame Allena for the scandal. Germaine might even block Allena from entering the family permanently.
August's chest he heave. The veins in his neck bulged against his skin.
He looked at Simon, who was hovering in the hall,gesturing frantically toward the elevators. Time was running out.
August let out a feral growl of pure, unadulterated frustration.
He stormed back to the desk. He snatched the Montblanc pen from where it had rolled near the edge.
He didn't look at the pages. He didn't read another word.
He violently flipped the thick stack of paper directlyto the last page.
Elisa's breath stopped. Her lungs burned. She kept her hand pressed firmly on the top edge of the paper,holding it steady for him.
August pressed the pen to the signature line.
The nib scratched aggressively against the premium paper. He signed his full, legal name-Augustus Baron Chambers IV-with violent, jagged strokes.
He pressed so hard on the final letter that the nib
snapped.
A thick drop of black ink splattered across the paper, flying up and hitting the pristine white cuff of Elisa's silk blouse.
August threw the broken pen onto the desk.
He leaned in close, his face inches from Elisa's. His breath was hot and smelled of coffee and rage.
"Take your goddamn house," August whispered,his voice vibrating with absolute hatred. "And get the hell out of my sight. You disgust me."
He turned and sprinted out of the office. Simon ran after him.
The heavy oak door slammed shut behind them.
The office plunged into a deafening,ringing silence.The only sound was the soft hum of the air conditioning vents.
Elisa stood frozen over the desk.
She slowly lowered her eyes to the final page of the document.
There it was.
The bold, aggressive signature. The black ink was still wwet, gleaming under the overhead lights.
It was done.
A massive, overwhelming wave of emotion crashed over her. It wasn't happiness. It was the agonizing,beautiful relief of a mother who had just pulled her child out of a burning building.
Her knees buckled. She grabbed the edge of the
desk to keep from collapsing. She closed her eyes,and a single, hot tear slipped down her cheek,splashing onto the mahogany wood.
You're safe, Kayden. He can never touch you.
Elisa opened her eyes. The vulnerability vanished,instantly replaced by the cold, calculating precision of Faye.
She carefully picked up the document, ensuring the ink didn't smear. She slid it back into the brown leather envelope and locked the clasp.
She turned and walked out of the office,ignoring the stares of the terrified executives in the hallway.
She got into the elevator and pressed the button for the underground parking garage.
She had the signature. But in the realm of billionaire divorces, a signature could be contested.He could claim he signed under duress.
She needed the final lock. She needed the physical manifestation of his absolute consent.
She needed the Chambers family seal. And she knew exactly where it was.
###Chapter 29
The taxi dropped Elisa off in the subterranean parking garage of the Manhattan penthouse building.
She bypassed the main lobby and walked directly to the private, biometric elevator. She pressed her thumb against the scanner. The light turned green.
She still had access. August, in hisarrogance and distraction, hadn't revoked her security clearance yet.
The elevator doors opened directly into the silent,sprawling penthouse.
The air inside was cold and smelled faintly of chemical cleaners.
Elisa stepped into the foyer.
"Mr. Chambers?" a nervous voice called out.
Brenda the housekeeper stepped out from the main hallway, her face paling when she saw it was Elisa. "Mrs. Chambers," she corrected herself,her hands wringing a dusting cloth. "I wasn't expecting you."
Elisa noticed the defensive posture immediately,but she didn't care.
"I'm just here to get some remaining paperwork,"Elisa said smoothly, walking past the terrified housekeeper without a second glance.
She walked straight into August's private study.
She closed the heavy door behind her and locked it.
She walked behind the massive mahogany desk and crouched down. She opened the bottom right drawer. Inside was a secondary, hidden biometric safe built directly into the wood.
Elisa placed her thumb on the scanner. It clicked open.
Inside the velvet-lined steel box sat a heavy,solid gold embosser. It was the official Chambers family seal, used only for irrevocable trust transfers and binding family contracts.
Elisa pulled the brown envelope from her bag. She took out the signed document and flipped to the last page.
She positioned the bottom right corner of the paper-right next to August's wet signature-between the heavy gold plates of the embosser.
She pressed down with both hands.
The metal groaned.
When she released the handle, a perfect,raised,three-dimensional crest of the Chambers family was permanently crushed into the fibers of the paper.
It was the ultimate legal kill shot. No lawyer on earth could argue that a document bearing both his signature and the locked family seal was signed by accident.
Elisa smiled. A cold, terrifying smile.
She put,the seal back, locked the safe, and slid the document into her bag.
She turned to leave the study.
Suddenly, the heavy front doors of the penthouse banged open.
Elisa stopped dead. She pressed herself against the wall next to the slightly ajar study door,peering through the narrow crack.
August strode into the foyer.
He was carrying Allena in his arms, bridal style.
Allena was wearing a hospital gown covered by August's expensive suit jacket. Her right ankle was wrapped in a thick, white fiberglass cast.
She had her arms wrapped tightly around August's neck,her face buried in his chest.
"I've got you, baby," August murmured, his voice thick with a tender, protective warmth that made Elisa's stomach churn. "You're safe now."
Brenda rushed forward, her hands fluttering nervously.
"Mr. Chambers!" Brenda gasped, her eyes darting frantically toward the closed study door. "Sir,you're back. Mrs. Chambers was just here to collect some of her remaining personal items. She left only a moment ago."
"The hospital was a circus," August snapped,shifting Allena's weight, his mind clearly elsewhere.
"The paparazzi were everywhere. I'm not letting her recover in a public ward. Did you change the mattress in the master bedroom to the medical-grade memory foam like I asked?"
"Yes, sir," Brenda stammered, sweating profusely.Allena lifted her head from August's chest. She looked around the cold, modern penthouse. A sly,victorious smile touched her lips.
"It's so beautiful, August," Allena whispered,kissing his jaw. "I just wanted to be in our home."
Our home.
Standing in the shadows of the study, Elisa felt a sudden, overwhelming urge to laugh.
This penthouse had been her prison for seven years.It was a sterile museum where she had slowly suffocated under his neglect. And now, this pathetic woman was claiming it as her ultimate prize.
Elisa looked at the heavy bag slung over her shoulder. She had the only thing of value in this entire cursed building.
She waited until August carried Allena down the hallway and disappeared into the master bedroom.
Elisa slipped out of the study. Her footsteps were completely silent on the hardwood floor.
She walked swiftly toward the front door.
Just as her hand grasped the heavy brass handle,a voice echoed from the hallway.
"August?" Allena called out from the bedroom,her voice suddenly sharp. "Is someone out there? I saw a grey coat."
August's heavy footsteps immediately pounded down the hallway.
Elisa didn't run. She calmly pulled the door open,stepped into the elevator, and hit the lobby button.The penthouse door swung wide open. August stood in the frame, his chest heaving, his eyes scanning the empty foyer.
He looked at the elevator. The digital display above the doors was dropping rapidly. PH... 40...39...
August stared at the descending numbers.
He knew it was her.
A strange, hollow sensation suddenly expanded in his chest. It felt like the air pressure in the room had dropped.
He had his mistress in his bed. He had his penthouse.He had his power.
But as he watched those numbers drop, he felt an inexplicable, terrifying certainty that he had just lost something massive, something he could never,ever get back.

###Chapter 30


Three days later.

The Pierre Hotel on the Upper East Side was a fortress of wealth and political power. Black SUVs lined Fifth Avenue, and a small army of private security kept the flashing cameras of the press at bay.

Tonight was the Chambers Family Foundation's political fundraiser for Senator Hayes.

A sleek, black Aethel corporate car pulled up to the curb.

Elisa stepped out.

She was wearing a custom, floor-length black velvet gown. The front was a severe, high-necked silhouette, projecting absolute armor. But the back plunged dangerously low, exposing the pale, flawless curve of her spine. Around her neck rested a heavy,antique emerald pendant, its facets catching the light with a cold, green fire. It was a piece Alastair had
insisted she wear, provided by Aethel's corporate jeweler to ensure their Chief Technology Architect looked the part. She touched the icy gemstone at her throat. Germaine had explicitly commanded her to wear the Chambers diamonds, a glittering leash meant to signal ownership. This vibrant, defiant emerald was her silent, absolute answer.

She looked like royalty. She looked lethal.

She walked up the steps and entered the grand ballroom.

The room was packed with billionaires, politicians,and socialites. The moment Elisa stepped onto the carpet, the ambient chatter dropped. Hundreds of eyes turned toward her,filled with malicious curiosity and whispered gossip.

Germaine Chambers materialized from the crowd instantly. She was wearing a diamond choker that looked like a glittering dog collar.

"You look acceptable," Germaine hissed in her ear,
keeping a fake smile plastered on her face for the cameras. "August is on the terrace. Go to him. Stand by his side. If any reporter asks, you tell them the rumors are lies and you are trying for a baby. Do not fail me."

Elisa looked down at Germaine's hand.

She didn't pull away. She just stared at the fingers until Germaine, feeling a sudden, inexplicable chill,let go.

Elisa turned and walked toward the massive French doors leading to the semi-enclosed stone terrace.

She wasn't here to play the wife. She was here because three major hospital directors were attending, and Alastair needed her to secure their data-sharing agreements for Project Chiron.

She picked up a flute of champagne from a passing waiter and walked toward the edge of the stone balustrade.

pillar, her footsteps slowed.

Standing in the dim light, partially hidden from the main ballroom, were August and Allena.

August was wearing a flawless tuxedo. He had Allena pinned gently against the stone pillar.

Allena was wearing a white lace gown. Her right foot was encased in a sleek, black medical walking boot.She had both hands resting flat against August's chest, her face tilted up toward his.

Their faces were inches apart. The sexual tension was thick and heavy. August was leaning in, his eyes dark with desire, about to kiss her right there, ten feet away from a room full of reporters.

Elisa stood perfectly still.

She watched them. She waited for the familiar sting of betrayal, the sharp pain in her chest that used to cripple her.

She felt absolutely nothing. It was like watching two strangers in a bad movie.

"Well, look what we have here. Still clinging on, are we?"

"What are you still doing here?" Tiffany drawled, her voice loud enough to carry over the music from inside. "Allena is going to be the next Mrs. Chambers.Everyone knows it. You're just...expired. Get out!"

The music inside seemed to pause. Several wealthy guests stepped out onto the terrace, drawn by the shouting.They stood in a semi-circle, watching with cruel, eager eyes, waiting for Elisa to break down and cry.
August frowned, but he didn't step forward. He didn't reprimand the woman. He didn't defend his wife. He simply stood in front of Allena, shielding her from the drama, silently endorsing the humiliation.

Allena peeked out from behind August's broad shoulder. A smug, triumphant smirk was plastered across her face.

Elisa didn't look at August. She didn't look at Allena.

She stared at the woman's vapid face, observing the sheer, unadulterated entitlement radiating from her expensive frame. Then, her eyes shifted to August,who stood there like a silent monolith, entirely complicit in this grotesque display. He was a man who demanded absolute perfection from everyone around him, yet here he was, actively shielding a woman whose friend was throwing a tantrum at a high-society political gala. The hypocrisy was staggering, a foul stench that permeated the crisp
night air. She watched Allena reveling in the protection she had stolen, playing the fragile victim while her friend did the dirty work. The absolute absurdity of it all crystallized in Elisa's mind. They were a pathetic ecosystem feeding off each other's worst traits.

"After all," Elisa whispered, "bitches and dogs are a match made in heaven."

She turned her back on them. The heavy black velvet of her gown flared out in a perfect, dramatic arc.

She walked out of the ballroom, out of the hotel, and into the cold New York night, leaving August Chambers burning in the ashes of his own ruined pride.
###Chapter 31


Elisa pushed through the heavy, gold-plated revolving doors of the Pierre Hotel.

"Elisa!"
August's voice was a low, vibrating roar. It carried
over the hum of the idling engines on Fifth Avenue.

A cruel, triumphant smile spread across his face.He took a step back, holding the phone high out of her reach.

"Hit a nerve, did l?" August mocked, his eyes gleaming with the thrill of the catch. "Let's see who you're really working for."

lawn.

He was going to force the phone to prompt for a passcode, or worse, he might accidentally trigger the facial recognition if he pointed it at her.

If he saw that picture clearly. If he saw those eyes.

Elisa's brain bypassed all logic. The maternal survival instinct, raw and violent, took complete control of her nervous system.

She didn't try to jump up and grab the phone. He was too tall. He was too strong.

CRACK.

The sound was deafening. It sounded like a gunshot echoing off the stone walls of the hotel.

The heavy brass edge of the ashtray slammed directly into the center of the smartphone screen.The impact was so violent that the kinetic shockwave traveled straight down August's arm.

The reinforced glass screen didn't just crack. lt exploded.

Tiny shards of sharp glass sprayed outward,catching the streetlights like deadly glitter.

intense vibration numbed his fingers. His hand sprang open involuntarily.

She brought her foot down with a desperate, frantic force.

She drove the steel spike of her heel somewhere into the center of the ruined device. She wasn't aiming for a specific component; she was just trying to kill it.

Crunch.

She twisted her ankle blindly, grinding her heel deep into the internal components, feeling the plastic casing snap and the microchips splinter under the pressure. The screen, or what was left of it, went
completely,permanently black.

She lifted her foot and stomped down again. And again. Her movements were chaotic, driven by pure terror, not precision. She didn't stop until the sleek piece of technology was reduced to a twisted,unrecognizable pile of plastic, glass, and bent metal.

She stood over the wreckage, her chest heaving violently. Her breath came in ragged,shallow gasps.

The street was dead silent.

The valet attendant was staring at her, his mouth hanging wide open. Several wealthy guests who had been waiting for their cars were frozen on the steps,staring in absolute shock.

August stood completely paralyzed.

He looked at the destroyed phone on the ground,and then he slowly looked up at Elisa. His eyes were wide with a mixture of disbelief and genuine,creeping horror.

He had expected her to cry. He had expected her to beg.

He never expected her to turn into a violent,
destructive force of nature right on Fifth Avenue.

Slowly, the shock on August's face morphed into a dark,twisted sneer.

He let out a harsh, barking laugh.

"You are completely insane," August breathed,pointing a shaking finger at the pile of trash on the ground. "You just destroyed a two-thousand-dollar phone like a psychotic animal. Whoever this guy is,you must be terrified I'll find him. You're pathetic."

Elisa looked down at her hands.

A sharp piece of flying glass had grazed her right index finger. A small, bright red bead of blood was welling up on her pale skin.

She stared at the blood.

The suffocating panic in her chest slowly began to recede. The cold, clinical logic of her mind booted back up.

The phone was dead. The data was encrypted and now physically inaccessible. The photo was gone.

Kayden was safe.
Elisa let out a long, slow exhale. Her shoulders dropped. The tension drained out of her muscles.

She calmly opened her black leather clutch. She pulled out a small, white tissue.

She wrapped the tissue around her bleeding finger,pressing down firmly to stop the blood. She didn't look at August while she did it. She treated the wound wvith the detached efficiency of a nurse.

Then, she slowly raised her head.

Her eyes met his. The panic was entirely gone. They were back to being pools of black ice.

"Like | said, August," Elisa said, her voice perfectly smooth and quiet. "Your imagination is pathetic. You should write cheap paperback novels. It suits your intellect."

She turned away from him.
